The Liberal Democrats want to expand apprenticeships and develop national colleges for vocational skills, aiming to end the "snobbery" about apprenticeships. UKIP plans to introduce an option for students to take an apprenticeship instead of four non-core GCSE subjects, while scrapping tuition fees for some students taking degrees in high-demand vocational subjects. The Green Party plans to expand apprenticeships by increasing funding and providing an apprenticeship to all qualified young people aged 16-25 who want one. The SNP has pledged to provide 125,000 "modern" apprenticeships in the next parliament, and Plaid Cymru supports the European Union's Youth Jobs Guarantee and wants to promote higher level apprenticeships and in-work learning for young people and adults.  Now, let's evaluate the assistants' answers:  Assistant A's answer is concise and summarizes the main points of the article. It covers the opinions and ideas of all the political parties mentioned in the article, which is relevant to the prompt. However, it lacks some details and specific information mentioned in the article, such as the budget for Labour's scheme and the specific vocational subjects mentioned in UKIP's plan.  Assistant B's answer is more detailed and includes more specific information from the article. However, it is not as concise as Assistant A's answer and seems to be a direct copy of parts of the article. It also lacks a clear summary or overview of the main points, making it harder to follow.  Considering the evaluation criteria, I would say that Assistant A's answer is more concise and relevant to the prompt, while Assistant B's answer is more detailed but lacks conciseness and clarity.  Therefore, Answer (a) is better.

Here is my own answer to the prompt:  The article discusses the opinions and ideas of different political parties in the UK regarding apprenticeships. The Conservatives plan to create 16,000 new apprenticeships and want to pay for it with money saved from benefits caps. Labour has pledged to create 80,000 more apprenticeships and provide better careers advice for teens. The Liberal Democrats want to expand apprenticeships and develop national colleges for vocational skills. UKIP has pledged to introduce an option for students to take an apprenticeship instead of four non-core GCSE subjects. The Green Party would expand apprenticeships by increasing funding and provide an apprenticeship to all qualified young people aged 16-25 who do not have one and want one. The SNP has pledged to provide 125,000 "modern" apprenticeships in the next parliament and wants as many of the new jobs as possible to be in emerging high-tech industries. Plaid Cymru wants to promote higher level apprenticeships and in-work learning for young people and adults. Lord Stevens defines collusion as ranging from the failure to keep records to agents being involved in murder. Peter Cory's definition includes secret cooperation and turning a blind eye to wrongful acts. The Billy Wright inquiry panel emphasizes the essence of collusion as an agreement or arrangement to achieve an unlawful or improper purpose. Al Hutchinson requires an agreement between parties and sufficient evidence to establish deliberate acts or omissions. Sir Christopher de Silva adopts a working definition similar to the Billy Wright inquiry panel, emphasizing that omissions must be deliberate. Irish judge Peter Smithwick's definition aligns with Peter Cory's, including both active acts and omissions or failures to act.  Now, let's evaluate the answers provided by the two AI assistants. Here is my own answer to the prompt:  The founding story of MercadoLibre began in 1999 when Marcos Galperin, inspired by eBay, created an online marketplace and auction house for Latin America. Galperin, a native of Buenos Aires, had studied for an MBA at Stanford University in California, where he came up with the idea. He pitched the idea to a private equity boss, John Muse, during a car ride, and secured his first investor. With the help of friends, including Pedro Arnt, who is now the company's chief finance officer, Galperin launched MercadoLibre in Argentina. In 2001, eBay bought a 19.5% stake in MercadoLibre, agreeing not to enter Latin America for at least five years, allowing MercadoLibre to dominate the region. Despite facing economic challenges, the company continued to grow, and in 2007, it floated shares on New York's Nasdaq exchange. Here is my own answer to the prompt:  The Victorian photographic method used by Jack Lowe is called ambrotype, which involves coating a glass plate with chemicals and exposing it to light through a 110-year-old camera. The process requires the camera's shutter to remain open for longer in low light conditions, resulting in exposures of up to 12 seconds. The image is then developed using a fixative, which sets the picture. The entire process must be started and finished within 15 minutes, making it a slow and deliberate process that requires willing participation from the subject. My answer: Prosopagnosia is a condition where people cannot recognize faces, even of those they know well. They can see individual facial features, such as the eyes, nose, and mouth, but cannot process them as a whole, making it difficult to recognize gestures and emotions. There are two main forms of prosopagnosia: developmental, which affects around 2% of the population, and acquired, which is much rarer and caused by specific brain damage. To evaluate the quality of the responses provided by the two AI assistants, I will first generate my own answer to the prompt.  My answer: UNICEF played a vital role in India's polio eradication efforts by establishing the Social Mobilisation Network for polio in 2001, which addressed resistance against the polio vaccine. The network focused on promoting hand-washing, hygiene, sanitation, exclusive breastfeeding, diarrhoea management, and routine immunization. UNICEF also partnered with the Indian government, Rotary clubs, WHO, and millions of front-line workers to implement innovative strategies, micro-plans, and seamless partnerships to cover the last mile in the battle against polio. Furthermore, UNICEF supported the introduction of the bivalent oral polio vaccine in 2010, which protected against both type 1 and type 3 poliovirus transmission. UNICEF continues to support India's efforts to ensure that children remain protected against polio until the disease is eradicated globally. Here is my own answer to the prompt:  The key statistics regarding fire staff's mental health issues mentioned in this article are:   * The number of UK fire and rescue staff taking long-term sick leave due to mental illness has risen by nearly a third over the last six years, from 600 to 780 cases. * In London, the figure has doubled since 2011-12, with 103 fire staff taking mental health leave this year, some after working at Grenfell Tower. * At least 126 staff have left the service due to mental health issues since 2011. * In 2016-17, 97 Scottish fire staff and 111 Northern Ireland fire staff took long-term mental health sick leave. * A survey of over 1,600 staff and volunteers across emergency services shows nearly nine in 10 have experienced stress, low mood or poor mental health while working in their current role, and 25% of them had contemplated suicide. Here is my own answer to the prompt:  The quoted persons and their views in the article are:  * Dr. Sunil Shah of St George's at the University of London, who explains that bereavement can have a direct effect on the health of the heart, citing a study that found the number of people who had a heart attack or stroke in the month after a loved one died was double that of a non-grieving control group. * The British Heart Foundation, which states that "broken heart syndrome," or stress cardiomyopathy, is a temporary condition where the heart muscle becomes suddenly weakened or stunned, often brought on by a shock such as bereavement or other significant emotional or physical stress. * Johns Hopkins University, which publishes an FAQ on broken heart syndrome, stating that most heart attacks occur due to blockages and blood clots, while cardiomyopathy does not.  Now, evaluating the assistants' answers:  Both answers (a) and (b) correctly summarize the views of Dr. Sunil Shah and the British Heart Foundation. However, answer (b) provides additional information from Johns Hopkins University, which is relevant to the topic and provides more context to the concept of "broken heart syndrome." This makes answer (b) more comprehensive and informative.  In terms of conciseness, both answers are clear and to the point, but answer (b) is slightly longer due to the additional information.  There is no creativity or novelty required in this prompt, as it is a straightforward summary task.  There is no missing important information in either answer, but answer (b) provides more context and depth to the topic.  Therefore, Answer (b) is better.
